< review>
I'm new to adventure motorcycles.  I bought a T700 about six months ago.  I've been riding it as much as I can, but still haven't quite gotten comfortable riding in dirt.  I signed up for a 3 hour class with Daniel which I completed a few days ago.  The class was excellent!  Daniel started with the basics of foot/peg and leg position.  During drills he stopped me often and gave me feedback which I greatly appreciated.  We then moved into body and arm position and continued to practice.  Daniel made some adjustments on my handlebar positioning that help me better position my arms and body on the motorcycle while standing up.  Toward the end of the class we worked on rear braking / sliding which was a lot of fun and confidence building.  Finally, we went on a single track.  Despite being a lot more difficult, I felt very confident riding the trail! Daniel did a super job and I expect to be returning soon for another session<//review>

<Time>1597077734333< /Time><Rating>5< /Rating>< Text>
I'll start this review by saying don't look anywhere else, book with Sedlak Offroad School, Daniel and his team get a 100% endorsement form me.

Sedlak Offroad School is unmatched if you want to learn how to ride an off-road bike or even how to ride a bike. Daniel and his team are awesome. You are being taught by the best, with a lifetime of competitive off-road experience Daniel takes you through a step by step process from starting out to preparing yourself for your first competition!

I honestly can't say enough good things about the experience. S.O.S. use brand new bikes, in the best condition, with top of the line apparel, helmets, goggles, gloves the works. I had never been off-road before, so I arrived somewhat nervous, but Daniel immediately put me at ease, and in the space of 4 hours, I'd gone from 100% novice to competent off-road rider. We started with a rundown of the bike I was going to be riding, then practiced starting the bike and riding off. This progressed into riding around cones to get used to the weight and how to balance the bike. When I was more comfortable with the bike, we practiced hard stops (without stalling!).

With all of this under our belts, we progressed to riding simple trails, that as the time went by progressed into more complex and challenging trails. The highlight was the last part of the session in which we followed Daniel on a ride that took us on inclines and declines, through streams, over rocky ground, loose ground, and all manner of terrain.

I finish this review by saying I'll be taking more coaching from Daniel. in the months to come.< /Text>

<rating>5<//rating>< Text>
I can't wait to move in! Disclaimer: Lease starts mid month, review is based on service to date and informal, self-directed property tour. If there is cause to update review after move in then I will, but as of now super excited to call Avalon Walnut Ridge my future home.

Service: Sylvia has been incredible. Seriously. I couldn't imagine a more attentive, thoughtful and professional point of contact. Responsive, personalized and helpful assistance.
Simply put, she's awesome!

Grounds: Coming from a *luxury* complex in San Ramon that has seen better days and is now horribly mismanaged/outdated despite being located in a highly expensive, suburban area. Walnut Ridge by comparison was far cleaner, updated and possessed better amenities based on value. So much gorgeous and well manicured greenery!

Unit: Spacious and renovated Modern Collection studio, see pics with labeled detail. Also, please note property map. Its extremely helpful when choosing a unit depending on preference. For example, I prioritized hard surface flooring (currently available in first floor units only), updated appliances and at least a partial nature view from the balcony vs. solely looking toward another building. If you aren't sure about specific unit amenities or location simply inquire.

Area: Safeway, Target, Century 14, Starbucks, Restaurants, Iron Horse Trail, Pleasant Hill Bart, 680 access etc., all within a 10 minute walk or drive. Perfect!

Potential Cons: Perfection is an illusion. Period. Figure out whether the cons outweigh the pros and go from there. Here's my list based on touring and reading past reviews.
1.) Buildings with certain units directly across from Bart tracks (107, 109, 997...)may come with an uncomfortable noise level. Choose wisely based on personal needs.
2.) As with any pet friendly environment you will have tenants who do not pick up after or follow guidelines for their pets. Sucks, thats life.
3.) Car Break-Ins, this one is pretty concerning. When walking around its not hard to see how this consistently happens, anyone can slip into the garages from off the street. Honestly, I'm wondering if it might be better to park in the open by the leasing office rather than the assigned underground space.
4.) Homeless Issue - This is a factor but its one prevalent in most major urban areas, especially with Bart being close.
5.) Water/Garbage not included. This will be an adjustment, however, since this community is roughly $300 less monthly than my last residence and has far better amenities its hardly a deal breaker.

Thats all I have for now, take care and stay safe!< /Text>

<text>First review but will update after I move in! Huge thank you to Salvador Millado (Sal), he is the most professional, kind, fun, direct, efficient, and transparent community consultant I have ever worked with and I have lived in over 3 countries and 6 different U.S. states. He is very knowledgable of the property and will go out of his way to accomodate you and answer all of your questions!

Avalon Walnut Ridge was the first complex in WC I looked at with my family and we were all in awe at first sight and this was not even the Premier back/gated side yet! I was pretty much sold already.  I needed to be close to BART as my husband will be working in SF, and me close to the highway as I'll be commuting to Antioch. This place was close enough to both but tucked away in a foresty like area that seemed very secure, safe and quiet.  To give all the other complexes (and myself) a fair chance I looked at over 5 others: Avalon walnut creek, AVE, Vaya, Arroyo, Avalon Eaves, and Lyric. The apartments closer to WC downtown (AVE, Lyric, Vaya) were nice but a lot more expensive and also could get pretty noisy. Living closer to the WC/Pleasant Hill border made more sense with downtown a 10 min drive away.  Avalon Walnut Creek was probably my second choice given proximity to BART and retail shops right below you however there was a lot of traffic noise, and I found working with the leasing office not to be as easy or smooth.  I made a second visit to Avalon walnut ridge but this time saw the back units where it is gated and with elevators as well as a jacuzzi, fitness center, wifi lounge and BBQ areas. It felt more like home, was SO quiet (could hear birds chirping!) and could only hear the BART station outside of the apartment and as you walk further away, as the apartment has double pane windows to block out sound pretty well.  The view of the courtyard with pool and jacuzzi could not be beat! The elevators going directly from the basement parking to my floor made it convenient as far as safety and moving things to and from my car.  The amazon hub for packages is nearby as well as mailboxes so I will never have to worry about my packages getting lost.   The appliances and finishes of the apartment are very modern, clean and just as nice as some of the other newer apartments in downtown walnut creek but at a little over half the price.  My husband likes to eat out and walk a lot, the retail shops at Avalon Walnut Creek and starbucks is about a 7 min walk, and the Iron Horse trail seems really nice to walk the kids or dogs around and I found it to be a very family and pet-friendly community. From what I understand the Iron Horse trail takes you to downtown walnut creek as well about a 30-40 min walk or 10 min drive which seems like a nice thing to do on the weekends or after work!

All in all, I think I found the perfect place to live and if it was not for Sal being so prompt, direct and welcoming this decision could have been a lot harder! < text>
I own a mail order business requiring daily deliveries, pickups and occasional visits to the post office.  As my company has grown over the years I have moved it from city to city.  The Gardena Post Office is now the 5th PO I have worked with.

This is the worst PO by a long shot.  Although the people working the windows and deliveries are perfectly nice people they are totally mismanaged.  For some reason that escapes me there are 5! different people in that office with the title "Postmaster".  Additionally, there are managers and supervisors.  I'm not sure if there are actually any official workers.  This all indicates that there are way too many chiefs and far too few indians.

The delivery/pick-up people are so poorly managed that they frequently simply skip us when they are running behind.  When you go to the post office the lines are always incredibly long.  Picking up a package at the PO is always a half-day task because they can never find anything in the back in a timely manner.

Oh yes, and try phoning them sometime.  They almost never answer the phone.  If you are wondering why, it is because the person responsible for answering the phone is also the main window clerk.  Unfortunately, the window and the phone are about a 2-3 minute fast walk apart from each other.  And the phone cannot be heard from the window area.  Another example of bad management.

As a business owner I know that when an operation like the Gardena PO is not working properly it is typically the fault of management. If I was asked to take over the management of this office I would keep almost all of the people and dump every one of the so-called managers, supervisors and postmasters.< /text>
